    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_271642667" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271642667" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4979538-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520654483p2/4979538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271642667?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/4979538-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12925064-inescapable">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Hush, Hush, Existence, and Twilight fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979538-erin?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979538-erin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979538-erin?shelf=ya-pnr-favorites">ya-pnr-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979538-erin?shelf=autographed-books">autographed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979538-erin?shelf=books-that-changed-your-life-and-ma">books-that-changed-your-life-and-ma</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271642667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9966591899198734582">OH holy crap was this story awesome!!!! I'm a huge fan of angel stories, and this one has earned itself a spot in my very top favorites because it had me HOOKED!!! <br/><br/>Evie is heading off to her first year of college, nervous to be leaving her Uncle and hating the fact that she won't know anyone but the awkward kid she met during her visit to the campus. So she's taken aback when the gorgeous and butterfly-enducing Reed Wellington practically accosts her and tells her she needs to leave the school. </span>
  <span id="freeText9966591899198734582" style="display:none">OH holy crap was this story awesome!!!! I'm a huge fan of angel stories, and this one has earned itself a spot in my very top favorites because it had me HOOKED!!! <br /><br />Evie is heading off to her first year of college, nervous to be leaving her Uncle and hating the fact that she won't know anyone but the awkward kid she met during her visit to the campus. So she's taken aback when the gorgeous and butterfly-enducing Reed Wellington practically accosts her and tells her she needs to leave the school. She can't figure out why he hates her so much when he's just meeting her, and as strange things start happening around her she can't help but turn to the boy she's inexplicably drawn to. Hottie country-boy quarterback Russell is determined to be there for her as she struggles, and she can't deny a strong attraction to him, too. Torn between destiny and a fate she chooses, Evie's world is torn apart as she learns what she really is and what it means for everyone around her. She may not have the final say in what her future holds, even with the help of some serious allies.<br /><br />First off, I absolutely LOVED Evie!! She's tough, strong, determined, and doesn't just sit around whining like some of the other heroines tend to do. I loved that Evie's already kind of bad-ass before she even starts to realize she's different; as an athletic, fairly outgoing, and daring heroine from the start, she is NO Bella Swan! When Reed confronts her, she sticks up for herself and doesn't let him push her around, and she is persistent about finding out what the magnetic pull to him means even if he's a total ass in the process. Part of what finally makes Reed change his mind about her (other than the butterflies he feels on his side) is how amazing this girl is; her bravery, witty comments, and determination win everyone over, me included!! Her friendships with Russell, Freddie, Buns, and Brownie showed off just how awesome a character she is, too, and I loved the banter between them and all of the fun moments they had together!! <br /><br />Reed and Russell....*sigh* oh, this is going to be tragic one way or another. Russell is introduced early on as a potential love interest, and Evie's clearly sweet on this hunky guy from the start. I wasn't as smitten b/c the whole country bumpkin lingo with him really didn't do him any favors, but I did love that he was always there for Evie. Reed, though, had my heart at first sight!! Oh, yes, he's an ass, but picture Alex Petyfer telling you in no uncertain terms that he wanted you to leave while your stomach did a million flips and something pulled you to him like a magnet and you'll see what I mean!!! He's sexy and cocky just like we all so love, and when Evie is badly injured during a field hockey incident and he scoops her up and takes her back to his place...I knew Evie and I were both goners!! *swoon* But, alas, as we all know, there must be romantic drama to keep these stories interesting. Evie is so torn between what her soul wants and what her other half can't live without. The play-out of the love triangle in Inescapable was something that I really, really liked, though. I normally hate them, and I suppose I'll have to wait until the last book of the series before I can say for sure what I think of how it turns out. But for those of us that love those relationships where jealousy and fate tear the beloved couple apart temporarily while our hearts break along with them, it was VERY well done in this book. It was just the perfect combo of heartbreak, jealousy, humor, catty enemies, butterfly-enducing moments, and her guy protecting her with all that he has even if it's killing him inside. I got sucked right into Evie and Reed's growing love for each other, and when Reed pushes her away to protect her it was crushing. One of my favorite scenes in this book was at a dance, where Russell, Reed, and Evie all go with their own dates and are forced to sit with each other at a table. When Reed and Russell are talking in front of Evie about their situation, and Reed uses a football play as an analogy (as if she can't figure out what he's talking about!), he tries to figure out why Russell didn't swoop in and take care of Evie when he had to let her go. He asks Russell why the 'other team' (Russell) didn't pick up the fumbled 'ball' (Evie), and they go back and forth about how the 'ball' was mangled (heartbroken)...it was so cute how Reed tried to protect her without being obvious, and there was some serious sparks going on between them as he sat next to her at that table!! Whew!! <br /><br />I've gone on and on about the romance blooming in this story, but Evie's discovery of what she and Reed really are and the dangers that come along with it are such an exciting part of this book. I think it's obvious from the cover that angels are involved, and let's just say Evie's very unique and therefore desired and/or feared by many!! What she is puts her in grave danger, and visions she has are terrifying her left and right. She knows something big is coming, and as she slowly figures out who's involved and what she needs to do, it throws everything into a tailspin. All of this leads up to a heartbreaking, gut-wrenching climax that had me at the edge of my seat, and even more unexpected twists that will lead into the rest of the series. I absolutely LOVE this story and these awesome characters, and I plan to dive right into Intuition so I can get back into Bartol's amazing world!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="9966591899198734582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review271642667">

<div id="review_800502591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/800502591" />
    <a title="Gabriela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14487453-gabriela"><img alt="Gabriela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578015171p2/14487453.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/800502591?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabriela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabriela" href="/user/show/14487453-gabriela">Gabriela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12925064-inescapable">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14487453-gabriela?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14487453-gabriela?shelf=angels-nephilim-demons">angels-nephilim-demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14487453-gabriela?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer800502591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17288894929857706161">I had just read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18845233.Under_Different_Stars__Kricket___1_' title='Under Different Stars (Kricket, #1) by Amy A. Bartol' rel='nofollow noopener'>Under Different Stars</a> and I thought that this lady, Bartol, has some good ideas running through her mind, even if she didnt do a great job executing them and perhaps this was better. But this was no different, no, scratch that; it was different, this was <i>worse.</i><br/><br/><b>This book started off in such monotonous way,</b> and it continued to be like that for over 70% of it. Just, unnaceptable. Not enough juice in the story and there is not one character that I can say "Dude, you are awesome" they</span>
  <span id="freeText17288894929857706161" style="display:none">I had just read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18845233.Under_Different_Stars__Kricket___1_" title="Under Different Stars (Kricket, #1) by Amy A. Bartol" rel="nofollow noopener">Under Different Stars</a> and I thought that this lady, Bartol, has some good ideas running through her mind, even if she didnt do a great job executing them and perhaps this was better. But this was no different, no, scratch that; it was different, this was <i>worse.</i><br /><br /><b>This book started off in such monotonous way,</b> and it continued to be like that for over 70% of it. Just, unnaceptable. Not enough juice in the story and there is not one character that I can say "Dude, you are awesome" they are all so one-dimensional, they follow a straight line of dialogue, without funny remarks, without any wit. Everytime somebody verbally attacked Evie she kept silent or responded something <i>lame.</i> And hardly anybody made a joke.<br /><br /><b>The relationships between the characters didnt have any build-up.</b> I mean, they were all besties or lovers or haters out of the freaking blue. All the sacrifice or devotion that you would have for someone with whom you had shared special moments existed, but it felt fake because precisely there werent any truly special moments to begin with.<br /><br />It goes without saying that the previous thing I said indicates that <b>there's some serious insta-cheese.</b> Oh, and how cheesy it is. Obsessing thoughts and outrageous declarations of love and oh my I choose you but I cant lose him either.<br /><br /><b>And what annoyed me the most?</b><br /><br />That freakishly horrible forced southern accent that Russell (One of the love interests) had. <br /><br /><i>"How are ya? I heard yer car broke down"</i><br /><br />Are you for real?<br /><br />How exasperating was reading this dude. And he talked to people with "y'all" when it should be "you". <i>Singular</i>.<br /><br /><i>OH MY GOODNESS,</i> Please somebody scratch my brain.<br /><br /><b>HOWEVER,</b><br /><br />Anytime I was like, <i>"Oh so that just magically happened"</i>, the author handed me an answer. So I have to say that <b>when it comes to plot holes, I dont believe there's any.</b> Im not necessarily saying that the plot was so rich and thick and full of details, because it was not. But, even if it was quite weak and transparent at least it was well done.<br /><br /><b>It irks me that there are some really good ideas in here, </b>and that this could have been such a great book. I was lured yet again by amazing ratings and reviews (Seriously, <i>HOW? </i>Were you all bribed with free books for a year and cookies?... And how do I get on that deal? *elevating my eyebrow*) <br /><br />So anyway, let's see if this get better, shall we? Because I already paid for the next 2 books- I know, Im a sucker for good ratings and an impulsive buyer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17288894929857706161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue">Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=demons">demons</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=why-must-i-torture-myself-so">why-must-i-torture-myself-so</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=i-almost-didn-t-finish">i-almost-didn-t-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096508092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15561778908715978079">Welp, that's what I get for going back to read an author's first book, I guess. It wasn't the worst thing I've ever read, but as other reviewers have pointed out, it IS very <i>Twilight</i>-esque. And that's not a selling point for me. Yet, I've really enjoyed the author's newer works, especially <i>Secondborn</i>, which just released. So, I thought, reasonably enough, that I'd probably enjoy her backlist. I even wasted my last Hoopla credit on the second book because the start of <i>Inescapable</i> was relatively a</span>
  <span id="freeText15561778908715978079" style="display:none">Welp, that's what I get for going back to read an author's first book, I guess. It wasn't the worst thing I've ever read, but as other reviewers have pointed out, it IS very <i>Twilight</i>-esque. And that's not a selling point for me. Yet, I've really enjoyed the author's newer works, especially <i>Secondborn</i>, which just released. So, I thought, reasonably enough, that I'd probably enjoy her backlist. I even wasted my last Hoopla credit on the second book because the start of <i>Inescapable</i> was relatively auspicious. But it's not to be. I can't force myself to listen to more of this love triangle, the constant declarations of love. I'm sure if I'd read this back when I read <i>Twilight</i>, I probably would have liked it. Maybe even really liked it. But I didn't, and so I don't.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9rSqmdNcl+knNRSHZBcPNPuJ6AmvuzgueaA4PaPbPt2thfxDPC6o7Zi98Cw/DyDvaDt9aWsdaldEHFgnwLxtUw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Bt3uNx2DWScCsCVTud+i6E9nmU+uUbPiengh/yEk/iBd7Ljt8vFmI704wfjix40z3NUML2r34ZtHxEHlQkOtrg==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText2601450909770052655" style="display:none">Author of the Secondborn Series:<br />Secondborn (Book 1)<br />Traitor Born (Book 2)<br />Rebel Born (Book 3) <br /><br />Author of the Premonition Series:<br />Inescapable (Book 1) <br />Intuition (Book 2)<br />Indebted (Book 3)<br />Incendiary (Book 4) <br />Iniquity (Book 5) <br /><br />Author of the Kricket Series:<br />Under Different Stars (Book 1) <br />Sea of Stars (Book 2)<br />Darken the Stars (Book 3)<br /><br />The Divided - A Science Fiction Romance short story, which is included in the Take Me To Your Reader: An Otherworld Anthology. <br /><br />Amy A. Bartol is the USA Today and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of The Secondborn Series, The Premonition Series, The Kricket Series, and a short story entitled “The Divided.” She has won numerous awards for her writing and been nominated for several more. She's a graduate of Hillsdale College, which inspired the setting of her Premonition Series. Amy lives in Michigan with her husband and two sons, but she travels often, sparking her imagination to create more worlds like the ones with hidden angels, doorways to alien landscapes, and fantastical futuristic societies and technologies.
